CONTRACT RENEW AL
Transmitting a Communication, dated November 22, 2000 from
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President, Cook County Board of Commissioners
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to renew contracts with Eugene Barnes and Stephen S.
Morrill whose names are submitted for consideration as County Lobbyists to serve for a period of one
year beginning December I, 2000 through November 30, 200 I , in the amount of $50,000.00 each, plus
expenses not to exceed $7,500.00 each (Accounts 490-260 and 018-260, respectively).
It is important that these individuals be approved as soon as possible in order to guarantee lobbying
services for the next General Assembly, which is set to convene in January 2001.

Commissioner Hansen, seconded by Commissioner Moreno, moved that the County Purchasing Agent be
authorized to renew the requested contracts. The motion carried unanimously.

COMMISSIONERS
PROPOSED ORDINANCE
Submitting a Proposed Ordinance sponsored by
WILLIAM R. MORAN, County Commissioner
PROPOSED ORDINANCE

COOK COUNTY MOBILE HOME LOCAL SERVICES TAX ORDINANCE
WHEREAS, the County of Cook is a home rule unit of local government, and as such has the
power to tax pursuant to Article VII, Section 6(a) of the 1970 1llinois Constitution;

7

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 5, 2000
WHEREAS, pursuant to the Mobile Home Local Tax Services Act, 35 ILCS 515/1 et seq., the
General Assembly has imposed a privilege tax upon owners of inhabited mobile homes, which applies to
all such mobile homes except those located within Cook County, which is exempted pursuant to Section
9.1 of that Act;
WHEREAS, the General Assembly specifically refused to limit a home rule county such as the
County of Cook from imposing its own tax at its own rate in Section 3 of the Act, 35 ILCS 515/3;
WHEREAS, revenue from the mobile home local services tax would be distributed by the County
Treasurer to the local taxing districts within the boundaries of which such mobile homes are located, in
the same proportion as the property taxes collectible for each such taxing district the prior year, and
would provide much needed revenue for these taxing districts to provide local services such as schools;
NOW THEREFORE BE IT ORDAINED, by the Board of Commissioners of Cook County:
Section:

Severability - Partial Invalidity.
Short Title.
Effective Date.

Section 1.

Mobile Home Defined

As used in thi s Ordinance, "mobile home" means a factory assembled structure designed for
permanent habitation and so constructed as to permit its transport on wheels, temporarily or permanently
attached to its frame, from the place of its construction to the location, or subsequent locations, and
placement on a temporary foundation, at which it is intended to be a permanent habitation, and situated so
as to permit the occupancy thereof as a dwelling place for one or more persons, provided that any such
structure resting in whole on a permanent foundation, with wheels, tongue and hitch removed at the time
of registration provided for in Section 4 of this Ordinance, shall not be construed as a "mobile home", but
shall be assessed and taxed as real property as defined by Section 1-130 of the Property Tax Code.
Mobile homes owned by a corporation or partnership and on which personal property taxes are paid as
required under the Revenue Act of 1939 shall not be subject to this tax. Mobile homes located on a
dealer' s lot for resale purposes or as an office shall not be subject to this tax.

8

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 5, 2000

Section 2.

Mobile home park defined

As used in this Ordinance, the phrase "mobile home park" means a tract of land or 2 or more
contiguous tracts of land which contain sites with the necessary utilities for 5 or more independent mobile
homes for a period of one or more months either free of charge or for revenue purposes, and s hall include
any building, structure, vehicle or enclosure used or intended for use as a part of the equipment of such
mobile home park. Separate ownership of contiguous tracts of land shall not preclude the tracts of land
from common licensure as a mobile home park if they are maintained and operated jointly. Neither a
mobile home resting on a permanent foundation, with wheels, tongue, lug bolts and hitch permanently
removed, nor a motorized recreational vehicle shall be construed as being a part of a mobile home park.

Section 3.

Imposition of Tax - Rate

Mobile homes in addition to such taxes as provided in the "Use Tax Act" and in the "New Motor
Vehicle and Trailers Sales Tax Ordinance" shall be subject to the following privilege tax only, and to no
ad valorem property tax. Except as provided in Section 8, the owner of each inhabited mobile home shall
pay to the Cook County Treasurer an annual tax of$.50 per square foot.
For purposes of this Ordinance, the square-footage shall be based upon the outside dimensions of
the mobile home excluding the length of the tongue and hitch. The owner of a mobile home on January I
of any year shall be liable for the tax of that year, commencing with January 1, 200 I .

Section 4.

Registration Form - Filing - Contents of Registration Form - Signature Misinformation - Application of Section

The owner of each inhabited mobile home located in Cook County on the effective date of this
Ordinance shall, within 30 days after such date, file with the county assessor a mobile home registration
form showing the name and address of the owner and every occupant of the mobile home, the location of
the mobile home, the year of manufacture, and the square feet of the mobile home based on the outside
dimensions of the mobile home excluding the length of the tongue and hitch together with the date that
the mobile home became inhabited, was initially placed in the county, or was moved to a new location.
The registration shall be signed by the owner or occupant of the mobile home. Mobile home park
operators shall forward a copy of the mobile home registration form provided in Section 5-303 of the
Cook County Mobile Home Park Ordinance, Cook County Ord. 5-291-5-312, to the County Assessor
within 5 days of the entry of such mobile home into such park. It is the duty of the County Assessor to
require timely filing of a properly completed registration for each mobile home located in Cook County.
Any person furnishing misinformation for purposes of registration or failing to file a required registration
is guilty of a Class B misdemeanor. This Section applies only when the tax permitted by Section 3 has
been imposed.

Section 5.

Delivery of Registrations to County Clerk

The County Assessor, within 7 days after filing of a registration, shal l deliver s uch registration to
the County Clerk.

9

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 5, 2000

Section 6.

Computation of Tax - Certification of Tax - Distribution to Local Taxing Units

Except as otherw ise provided in this Section, within 60 days of receipt of each registration form,
the County Assessor sha ll compute the tax due, as provided in Section 3, and certify the tax to the County
Treasurer who shall mail the tax bill to the owner of s uch mobile home at the time he receives the
certification or on the annual billing date, whichever occurs later, commencing on January 1, 2002. If the
registration fonn is accompanied by a receipt for privilege taxes paid in Illinois for the current tax year,
no further privilege taxes sha ll be imposed for the remainder of the current tax year. If the mobile home
is initia ll y harbored after the annual liability date, as provided in Section 3 of th is Ordinance, the County
Assessor shall red uce such tax 1/ 12 for each month that has passed since such annual liability date. A
mobile home harbored after the first day of such month shall be considered to have been harbored for the
entire month for the purposes of th is Section. Thereafter, the County Assessor shall compute such tax as
of the first day of January of each year and certify the tax to the County Treasurer. Such tax s hall be due
and payable to the County Treasurer within 60 days after the treasurer mails the tax bill to the address of
record. T he County Treasurer shall distribute such taxes to the local taxing districts within the boundaries
of which such mobile ho mes are located, in the same proportion as the property taxes collectible for each
such taxing district in the prior year.

Section 7.

Error in Tax bill - Affidavit by Owner

If a tax bill is in error as to the sq uare footage of the mobile home or as to the rate of tax, the
owner may file wi thin 6 months following receipt of the bill an affidav it with the county assessor setting
fo rth such error. If the tax bill does not show the name of the correct owner, the person whose name
appears as owner on the bill may file an affidavit with the county assessor so stating and id entify ing the
correct owner, if known. Upon the filing of an affidavit as provided in this Section, the County Assessor
shall issue a corrected bill and shall so indicate on his records.

Section 8.

Reduction of Local Services Tax - Application for Reduction

The local services tax for owners of mobile homes who (a) are actually residing in such mobile
homes, (b) hold title to s uch mobile home as provided by the " Il li nois Vehicle Code", approved
September 29, 1969, as amended and (c) are 65 years of age or older or are disabled persons within the
meani ng of Section 3. 14 of the "Senior Citi zens and Disabled Persons Property Tax Relief and
Phannaceutical Assistance Act," 320 ILCS 25/3. 14, on the annual billing date shall be red uced to 80
percent of the tax prov ided for in Section 3 of this O rdi nance. Proof that a claimant has been issued an
Illinois Disabled Person Identification Card stating that the claimant is under a C lass 2 disability, as
provided in Section 4A of The Illinois Identification Card Act, shall constitute proof that the person
thereon named is a disabled person within the meaning of this Ordinance. An application fo r reducti on of
the tax shall be filed with the County Assessor by the individual who is entitled to the red uction.
App li cation for the reduction in tax shall be done by submitting proof that the app licant has been iss ued
an Illinois Disabled Person Identificat io n Card designating the app licant's disability as a Class 2
disability, or by affidavit in s ubstantially the following form:

APPLICATION FOR REDUCTION OF MOBILE HOME LOCAL SERVICES TAX
I hereby make application for a red uction to 80% of the total tax imposed under the Cook County
Mobile Home Local Services Tax.

Section 9.

Delinquent Taxes - Lien - Notice - Force and Effect of Lien - Release

If any local services tax imposed by this Ordinance is not paid when due, the County Treasurer
shall have a lien on the mobile home for the amount of the tax, penalties and interest due. The Treasurer
shall notify the taxpayer in writing of the existence of the Iien. Such lien shall terminate unless the
County Treasurer files with the County Recorder a notice of lien, within one year of such tax date. From
the time of the filing, the amount set forth in the certificate also constitutes a lien upon all property of the
taxpayer then owned by him or thereafter acquired by him in the period before the expiration of the lien.
Such liens have the same force, effect and priority as a judgment lien and continue for 10 years from the
date of the recording unless sooner released or otherwise discharged. The County Treasurer may, at any
time, release all or any portion of the property subject to any lien provided for in this Ordinance or
subordinate the 1ien to other liens if he determines that the taxes are sufficiently secured by a lien on other
property of the taxpayer or that the release or subordination of the lien will not endanger or jeopardize the
collection of taxes.
lf the owner of a mobile home upon which the tax has not been paid does not
within 6 months after a lien has been filed, civil action may be instituted by the collector
of the tax, plus interest, penalties and costs. If sale of the property is ordered, the court
sale to be made in cash or on such terms as it may deem in the best interests of all parties.
direct that such sale be held by the sheriff or in open court.

for the amount

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 5, 2000

Section 10.

Interest on Delinquent Taxes - Penalty for Fraud

If any local services tax, or part thereof, imposed by this Ordinance is not paid on or before the
due date for such tax, interest on such amount at the rate of I Yi% per month shall be paid for the period
from such due date to the date of payment of such amount. If such failure to pay such tax is the result of
fraud, there shall be added to the tax as a penalty an amount equal to 50% of the deficiency.

Section 11.

Notice to County of Retail Sales

Mobile home dealers shall within I 0 days after any retail sale and delivery of a mobile home, notify
the County Assessor of the sale, the name of the purchaser, year of manufacture, the point at which delivery
to the purchaser was made, and the serial number and exterior meas urements of the mobile home.

Section 12.

Mobile Home Park Operators; Mobile Home Ownership Change; Notice

An operator of a mobile home park licensed under the provisions of the Cook County Mobile
Home Parks Ordinance, Cook County Ord. 5-291-5-312, shall notify the County Assessor when a change
in ownership occurs in a mobile home located within the operator' s park. Such notification shall include
the same information for the new owner as that contained in the registration form required of mobile
home park operators by Section 4 of this Ordinance.

Section 13.

Necessity of Permit Certifying Payment of Tax Prior to Moving Mobile Home Penalty

Before any mobile home subject to the tax imposed by this Ordinance may be moved, the
transporting company must obtain a permit issued by the County Treasurer certifying that the tax on the
mobile home has been paid for the current tax period and all previous tax periods for which taxes remain
due. It shall be a Class B misdemeanor for any person or entity to move any mobile home or cause it to
be moved a distance of more than one mile without having received such permit. It shall be a Class B
misdemeanor for any taxpayer to move any mobile home or cause it to be moved a distance of more than
one mile without such permit having been issued by the County Treasurer. This Section does not apply to
any person or entity who moves a mobile home or causes it to be moved pursuant to a court order, nor
does this Section apply to any person or municipality that moves a mobile home under the Abandoned
Mobile Home Act.

Section 14.

Violation of Ordinance - Penalty

It shall be a Class B misdemeanor to fail to submit information required under this Ordinance or
to knowingly submit any false information under this Ordinance.

Section 15.

Severability - Partial Invalidity

If any provision of this Ordinance or the application therefor to any person or circumstance is held
invalid, such invalidity does not affect other provisions or applications of this Ordinance which can be
given effect without the invalid application or provision, and to this end the provisions of this Ordinance
are declared to be severable. If any section, sub-section, sentence or clause of this Ordinance shall be
adjudged unconstitutional, such adjudication shall not affect the validity of the Ordinance as a whole or of
any section, sub-section, sentence or clause thereof not adjudged unconstitutional.

12

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 5, 2000

Section 16.

Short Title

This Ordinance shall be known and may be cited as the Cook County Mobile Home Local
Services Tax Ordinance.

Section 17.

Effective Date

This Ordinance shall be effective January I, 2001.

Commissioner Moran, seconded by Commissioner Daley, moved that the Proposed Ordinance be referred
to the Committee on Finance. (Comm. No. 240225). The motion carried unanimously.

years, The Chicago Bar Foundation, with the he lp of the C hicago Volunteer Legal Services Foundation
(CVLS), has managed the Guardianship Assistance Desk located on the tenth floor of the County
Admi nistration Building, at 69 West Washington Street. The Chicago Bar Foundation manages the desk
with volunteer attorneys. The fou ndation has relied solely on its own resources, assistance from CVLS
and outside grants, and has not received compensation from Cook County.
Reason:

The Guardianship Assistance Desk is available to help those who wish to represent themselves
in seeking to establish guard ianship fo r minors in the Probate Division of the Circuit Court of
Cook County. Volunteer attorneys counse l clients on guardianship law and help them prepare
necessary court papers with the assistance of court staff. In addition to personal assistance,
The Chicago Bar Foundation has developed self-help packets fo r those clients who w ish to
prepare their own papers. The Chicago Bar Foundation has received national recognition,
inc luding an award from the American Bar Association, for its work in assisti ng the public
with over I 2,000 guardianship petitions over the past five years.
Thi s contract is req uested to ensure the continuation of these important services. The contract
funds wil l be used to compensate CVLS for the management and staffing of the Guardianship
Assistance Desk on an on-going basis. The Chicago Bar Foundation and the CVLS have
pledge to match the value of the county' s contribution to the program.

Est imated Fiscal Im pact: $40,000.00. Contract period: December I , 2000 through November 30, 200 I.
(3 I 0-260 Account). Requisition No. 13 I 00002.

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioners Moreno and Silvestri, moved that the County
Purchasing Agent be authorized to enter into the requested contract. The motion carried unanimously.

* * * * *
Transmitting a Communication from
DONALD P. O' CONNELL, Chief Judge, Circuit Court of Cook County
requesti ng authorization for the Purchas ing Agent to enter into a contract with Lexis-Nexis, Inc., Dayton,
Ohio, a division of Reed Elsevier, Inc., for onli ne research services for Cook County. We make this
request on behalf of all Cook County departments and agencies that utilize these services as set forth on
the submitted schedule. Lexis-Nexis, Inc. currently provides these services to Cook County under County
Contract No. 98-41-900 which expires January 3 I, 200 I.

36

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 5, 2000
Reason:

For the past several months, representatives from the Office of the Chief Judge, the Office of the
State's Attorney and the Office of the Public Defender evaluated proposals submitted by both
Lexis-Nexis, Inc. and Westlaw, the only two major providers of online research services. This
committee unanimously recommended that the County maintain its relationship with LexisNexis, Inc. as the sole provider of online research services. The committee's recommendation is
based on several key factors, which include the high quality of service provided by Lexis-Nexis,
Inc. over the past several years, competitive pricing, significant price discounts on hard copy
publications, support of our users who access services through the county's AS/400 system and
the Lexis-Nexis, Inc. commitment to customized services. Also, Lexis-Nexis, Inc. has
committed to providing expanded services at lower costs over the next five years.
The proposed contract, with certain exceptions, provides unlimited access to the most
frequently used research libraries, unlimited training support, and printing, cite checking and
customized services. The fixed price for these services is $52,000.00 per month or
$1,872,000.00 for the three-year period beginning February I, 2001. Measured against the
County's current Lexis-Nexis, Inc. billings of $57,240.00 per month, this proposed contract
will save $5 ,240.00 per month, or $188,640.00 for the three-year contract period.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: $1,947,000.00. Contract period: February 1, 2001 through January 31, 2004.
(300-353 Account). Requisition No. 13000001.
The Chief Information Officer has reviewed this item and concurs with this recommendation.

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioners Moreno and Silvestri, moved that the request of
the C hief Judge of the Circuit Court of Cook County be approved, as amended and that the County
Purchasing Agent be authorized to enter into the requested contract. The motion carried unanimously.

by
JOHN J. ROBINSON, Undersheriff
requesting authorization to issue a Request for Proposal (RFP) for a professional service contract to
provide residential substance abuse treatment to addicted female detainees. This is the first year for the
Residential Substance Abuse Treatment program from the Illinois Criminal Justice lnfonnation Authority
(IC.TIA).

The qualified vendor will be requested to provide substance abuse treatment, including assessments,
individualized treatment plans, group counseling, individual counseling, skill building, recreational
activities and sober living.
The nature of these professional services, are such that they lend themselves to a Request for Proposal
process. The RFP will be managed in a manner to ensure that the needs and best interests of the addicted
female detainee and Cook County are met. For your infonnation and consideration, a copy of the RFP
has been submitted. This office in consultation with the ICJlA prepared the RFP.

bridge to avoid a fire, and as a result he injured his back (L5-S I bulging disc). The County
has paid zero in TTD benefits and $6,864.50 in medical expenses for a total of $6,864.50.
The County is entitled to recover 75% of that amount, which is $5, 148.38. The County has
agreed to accept $2,000.00 and waive $3, 148.38 of our lien in exchange for $1.00 lump sum
settlement contract. The Finance Subcommittee on Industrial Claims approved the lien
waiver and the $1.00 lump sum settlement on June 13, 2000. The Illinois Industrial
Commission approved the $1.00 contract on June 20, 2000. Therefore, we request Board
approval of our lien waiver and the settlement agreement involving a $1.00 lump sum
settlement. State's Attorney, Richard A. Devine, is submitting Industrial Comm ission Lump
Sum Petition and Order No. 97-WC-34129 in the amount of $1.00 and recommends its
payment. (Finance Subcommittee June 13, 2000). Attorney: Joseph A. Vitell, Law Firm of
Joseph A. Vitell & Associates, Ltd.

COMMISSIONERS HANSEN, MORENO AND SILVESTRI VOTED PRESENT ON
THE ABOVE ITEM.
COMMISSIONER QUIGLEY, SECONDED BY COMMISSIONER MORAN, MOVED
APPROVAL OF THE INDUSTRIAL COMMISSION CLAIMS. THE MOTION CARRIED.

approximately $150.00 to $180.00 based on services selected.

Management regarding Pre-Paid Legal Plans. These programs would provide employees
with optional assistance for their personal legal needs. Services include:







Unlimited legal consultations

Traffic violations
Legal document review
Financial planning assistance

present this opportunity to the employees of Cook County. They have a unique affi liation
with CNA Pre-Paid Legal Services, Inc., the largest provider of these plans nationwide. The
Advocate Group has compiled an in-house team specificall y tailored to the administrative
needs of the County for sales, enrollment, payroll and customer's services.

REPORT OF THE COMMITTEE ON PERSONNEL COMPLIANCE
November 14, 2000
The Honorable,
The Board of Commissioners of Cook County

ATTENDANCE
Present:

Chairman Moran, Commissioners Carr, Hansen, Moreno and Sims (5)

Also Present:

Commissioners Butler and Sutker (2); Mark Kilgallon - Chief, Bureau of Human
Resources; and Randy Johnston - State's Attorney's Office.

Absent:

Vice Chairman Schumann and Commissioner Maldonado (2)

Ladies and Gentlemen:
Your Committee on Personnel Compliance of the Board of Commissioners of Cook County met pursuant
to notice on Tuesday, November 14, 2000 at the hour of 11 :00 A.M. in the Board Room, Room 569,
County Building, 118 North Clark Street, Chicago, Illinois.
Your Committee has considered the following item and upon adoption of this report, the
recommendations are as follows:
235458

COOK COUNTY PERSONNEL RESlDENCE REQUIREMENT ORDINANCE
(PROPOSED ORDINANCE). Submitting a Proposed Ordinance sponsored by Calvin R.
Sutker, County Commissioner:

PROPOSED ORDINANCE
BE IT ORDAINED BY THE COOK COUNTY BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS
ARTICLE I
Section 1. Short Title: This article shall be known as the Cook County Personnel
Residence Requirement Ordinance.

118

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDI NGS FOR DECEMBER 5, 2000
Section 2. Purpose: To encourage each Cook County employee to maintain a personal
commitment to a residence in Cook County and to assure all residents that employees share
in the responsib ility of investing in the future of Cook County.
Section 3. Residency Requirement of All Cook County Employees: Upon the effective
date of this ordinance and thereafter, the County of Cook shall only em ploy persons who
maintain residence in Cook County throughout the ir employment. Wages, salary and
em ployee benefits may only be pa id to persons residing in Cook County.
Section 4. Exemption: Grandfather Clause: All present Cook County employees are
exempt from the provi sions of the residency requirements of this ordinance.
ARTICLE II
Section 1. Effective Date: This ordinance shall take effect immediately upon adoption.
NOTE:

This item was also referred to the Committee on Finance.
235457).

(See Comm. No.

*Referred to the Personnel Compliance Committee on 8/9/00.
*Deferred at the Personnel Compliance Committee Meeting of 10/ 10/00.

Chai rman Moran stated that letters were received from the Bureau of Health Services and the Bureau of
Human Resources and should be placed in the record.
Commissioner Hansen asked ifthere was a representati ve from the Bureau of Health Services?
Chairman Moran responded that there was no one present from the Bureau of Health Services.
Commissioner Hansen asked for a response from Mark Kilgallon regarding Ruth Rothstei n' s req uest that
the Board consider a provision that wo uld pennit the Bureau of Health Services to waive the res idency
requirement fo r categories of workers who are in short supply.
Mark Ki lgallon, Chief, Bureau of Human Resources, stated that he had spoken to Ruth Rot hstein and she
has asked that the waiver req uest be withdrawn.
Commissioner Hansen s uggested to the C hairman that Ruth Rothstein should put this new info rmation in
writing. He further said he favors the proposal s ponsored by Commissioner Sutker and he asked fo r the
deferral at the last meeting in order to receive more detailed information.
Mark Kilgall on stated that he wi ll get the request in writing.
Mark Kil gallon stated that the Bureau of Human Resources oversees approximately fifteen thousand of
the County's employees, which means that an add itional twelve thousand employees do not come under
the jurisdiction of the Bureau. He commented that his statements regardi ng Cook County hiri ng practices
only pertain to about sixty plus percent of the total number of employees. He further stated that elected
offi cial s have been notified of today's meeting and were asked to attend the meeting to address any
questions or concerns regard ing the proposed ordinance. He stated that he wanted to make it c lear that he
is only speaking for those departments under the President and the Bureau of Health Services, and not a
large part of the County that is not overseen by the Bureau of Human Resources.

11 9

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 5, 2000
Mr. Kilgallon stated that the Bureau of Human Resources surveyed a number of jurisdictions including
collar counties, and the majority of the counties do not have a residency ordinance. Will and McHenry
counties, however, do have ordinances.
Mr. Kilgallon further said the Bureau of Human Resources does not know what the impact the ordinance
will have on Cook County. He stated the Bureau will be able to do some analysis but because of the size
of the Cook County and its diversity, Human Resources cannot make the assumption that there will be
problems because some other jurisdictions are having problems. He continued by saying Human
Resources did a quantitative analysis on what impact the ordinance would have if everyone agreed to
move back into Cook County, and the assumption is there would not be an impact. However, if one
person does not move back into Cook County because of the residency requirement, then there still would
be a cost factor whether it means going to the second person on the eligibility list or whether it means
reposting and possibly doing more testing that would result in a fiscal impact to the county.
He stated that the fact of having county employees supporting county businesses, supporting county
schools, paying property taxes and living in the county, and benefits that have a financial gain to Cook
County.
Commissioner Hansen asked ifthere are articles or studies that have been done on the proposed residency
ordinance?
Mark Kilgallon responded that the Bureau of Human Resources is seeing some problems, which is one of
his concerns. He said the Bureau has not seen positive stories, and the county would have to look at other
jurisdictions that are having success with resindecy requirements.
Commissioner Hansen stated that a well-written aiticle will look at both sides of the matter-the cost
benefits and the cost disadvantages.
Mark Kilgallon stated he has one article he will distribute to the committee that addresses Commissioner
Hansen's request.
Commissioner Hansen asked what is the position of the administration on the residency ordinance?
Mark Kilgallon responded that the administration supports the ordinance.
Commissioner Carr stated that the residency ordinance will have an impact on the county, and it is tough
when someone makes his or her living in Cook County and pays taxes elsewhere. Personally, he stated
that the ordinance is not a bad thing.
Mark Kilgallon stated that anyone who applies for a position with the City of Chicago, must show that
they are a resident of the City of Chicago, which could limit recruitment. Mr. Kilgallon stated that the
State's Attorney's Office needs to look at the present language on the County's ordinance. He further
stated that he believes it would still allow the county to recruit from outside the county as long as they
have an established residency in Cook County by the time of employment. He continued by say ing that
occasionally a national search would need to be done for an expert and there currently is no stipulation in
the ordinance. The City of Chicago allows several months for new employees to establish residency
within the City after they are selected by a committee for specific positions. The residency ordinance
before the committee does not indicate those specifics and would be subject to interpretation on when it
actually goes into effect-whether by application or by employment.

120

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 5, 2000
Commissioner Hansen asked if there is language amending the ordinance to allow a period of time for an
employee to move into Cook County?
Mark Kilgallon stated that he can provide the committee with language, but the amendment has not been
discussed with the sponsor of the ordinance.
Commissioner Sutker stated that as sponsor of the ordinance, his intention was that residency would be
required upon employment and not upon application. He stated that Section 3 in the ordinance clearly
states the provision. He also said that Cook County wants a commitment from County employees as part
of their employment. Commissioner Sutker read portions of a Chicago Tribune newspaper article in
support of the proposed ordinance into the record.
Commissioner Butler stated he believes the reason for the proposed ordinance is because there are
employees who work for Cook County and live outside the county who are not paying property taxes. He
suggested a better idea would be to have a Cook County Employment Tax. He stated he finds it difficult
to tell people where they must li ve in order to be employed. He closed by saying that the ordinance is bad
policy and it destroys the concept of a regional form of government.
Commissioner Hansen restated his earlier requests. He concluded by saying that if the administration
believes the ordinance should include a contingency to allow employees a period of time to move into
Cook County, the commissioners should receive the suggested language before the board meeting.
Commissioner Moreno stated he agrees with Commissioner Butler, but he thinks the ordinance is not
necessary and believes the county can scrutinize employment applications no matter where the applicant
resides, provided they are qualified.
Commissioner Sims stated that the county should look at making exceptions and amendments if the
county begins to loose valuable employees or highly qualified applicants. The commissioner said she
believes the county should " leave the door open."

Commissioner Hansen moved approval of Item 235458, seconded by Commissioner Carr.
Commissioner Hansen called for a Roll Call, the votes of yeas and nays being as follows:
ROLL CALL ON MOTION TO APPROVE ITEM 235458
Yeas :

Chairman Moran, Commissioners Carr, Hansen and Sims (4)

Nays :

None (0)

Present:

Commissioner Moreno (I)

Absent:

Vice Chairman Schumann and Commissioner Maldonado (2)

Divided:

None (0)

The motion to approve CARRIED.
Commissioner Sims moved to adjourn the meeting, seconded by Commissioner Moreno.
motion carried and the meeting was adjourned.

235458 from the text of the Report of the Personnel Compliance Committee ofNovember 14, 2000. The

Residence Requirement Ordinance CARRIED.
01-0-2
ORDINANCE

Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE CALVIN R. SUTKER, COUNTY COMMISSIONER
BE IT ORDAINED BY THE COOK COUNTY BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS
ARTICLE I
Section 1.

Short Title:

This article shall be known as the Cook County Personnel Residence

Requirement Ordinance.

Section 2. Purpose: To encourage each Cook County employee to maintain a personal commitment to a
residence in Cook County and to assure all residents that employees share in the responsibility of
investing in the future of Cook County.

Section 3. Residency Requirement of All Cook County Employees: Upon the effective date of this
Ordinance and thereafter, the County of Cook shall only employ persons who maintain residence in Cook
County throughout their employment. Wages, salary and employee benefits may only be paid to persons
residing in Cook County. Any new employee shall have six (6) months from date of hire to establish
actual residency with Cook County.

Section 4. Exemption: Grandfather Clause: All present Cook County employees who reside outside
of Cook County upon adoption of this Ordinance are exempt from the provisions of the residency
requirements of this Ordinance.

Section 5. Administrative Rules and Regulations: The Chief, Bureau of Human Resources is
authorized to adopt promulgate and enforce Rules and Regulations and to administer and enforce this
Ordinance.

122

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 5, 2000

ARTICLE II
Section 1. Effective Date: This Ordinance shall take effect immediately upon adoption.
Approved and adopted this 5th day of December 2000.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DA YID ORR, County Clerk

Personnel Compliance Committee on November 14, 2000 be approved and adopted. The motion carried
unanimously.

CITY OF BLUE ISLAND (NO CASH BID REQUEST). Transmitting a Communication,
dated June 13, 2000 from Deborah Sims, Chairman, Tax Delinquency Subcommittee,
submitting a request from Donald E. Peloquin, Mayor:
Re: City of Blue Island

123

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 5, 2000
I am writing to you on behalf of the residents of the City of Blue Island. We are requesting
your assistance in securing tax delinquent properties on a no cash bid basis from the county
scavenger sale. These properties have been an eyesore for the residents that live next to them
for years. Our building department has tried numerous times to contact the property owner to
no avail. Some of the lots will be used for single family housing and we have a contractor
interested in building on the lots. We are also trying to secure an abandoned restaurant/store
which is in need of repair. The city would be seeking a RFP in regards to selling or giving
this property to an entity. My staff and I believe that a small grocery/deli store would be the
most productive use of the property. Two additional lots adjacent to a local church, would be
used for both commuter and church parking.
The City of Blue Island will retain legal counsel to obtain the tax deed and will bear all legal
and other costs associated with acquisition of the parcels.

BOBBIE L. STEELE AND CALVIN R. SUTKER, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
Recognition of
Oak Forest Hospital of Cook County's
90 Years of Service
WHEREAS, we recogni ze that Oak Forest Hospital of Cook County was responsibly established by the
Cook County Board of Commissioners as the last County Poor Farm in December of 1910 to serve
people in need; and
WHEREAS, Oak Forest Hospital's 90-year history has been an important part of Cook County
Government's 165-year commitment to the health and well being of County residents'; and
WHEREAS, Oak Forest Hospital has evolved into a dynamic and modern healthcare center governed by
the Cook County Board of Commissioners, and serving as an affi liate of the Cook County Bureau of
Health Services; and
WHEREAS, Oak Forest Hospital ' s mission of caring has developed into a unique healthcare center
devoted to the diagnosis, treatment, rehabilitation and Jong term care of disabled and older patients; and
WHEREAS, Oak Forest Hospital provides two contemporary levels of care in the Cook County Bureau
of Health Service's continuum of care, including Acute Care (medical surgery, intensive care, ventilator,
and inpatient rehabilitation) and Long Tern1 Care (subacute, skilled nursing care and intermediate care); and
WHEREAS, Oak Forest Hospital strengthens the mission and goals of the Cook County Ambulatory and
Communi ty Health Network with continuing support for south suburban Ambulatory Health Centers,
including Outpatient Rehabilitation services; and
WHEREAS, Oak Forest Hospital maintains accreditation from the Joint Comm ission on Accreditation of
Healthcare Organizations and the Commission on Accreditation of Rehabilitation Faci lities, and is
licensed by the Illinois Department of Public Health; and

127

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 5, 2000
WHEREAS, Oak Forest Hospital's long standing commitment to serving as a facility of learning has
included sixteen years of providing community-based work experience through the Transitional
Employment Program (TEP), for students from High School Districts 228 and 230; and
WHEREAS, for 90 years, thousands upon thousands of Cook County residents received quality services
and compassionate and dignified care at Oak Forest Hospital; and
WHEREAS, all who are served appreciate Oak Forest Hospital ' s rich history and fulfillment of its
important mission and commitment to the health of all Cook County residents, now
THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners recognizes Oak
Forest Hospital of Cook County for 90 years of service and healthcare leadership and;
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that Oak Forest Hospital of Cook County continues as a healthcare
provider and leader for the 21st Century.

RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE WILLIAM R. MORAN AND PRESIDENT JOHN H. STROGER, JR.
COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JERRY BUTLER, ALLAN C. CARR, EARLEAN COLLINS,
JOHN P. DALEY, GREGG GOSLIN, CARL R. HANSEN, TED LECHOWICZ,
ROBERTO MALDONADO, JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, MIKE QUIGLEY,
HERBERT T. SCHUMANN, JR., PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS,
BOBBIE L. STEELE AND CALVIN R. SUTKER, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, at 7:55 a.m. on Sunday morning, December 7, 1941 , 183 planes of the Imperial Japanese
Air Force attacked units of the armed forces of the United States stationed at Pearl Harbor; and
WHEREAS, the initial blow was a surprise attack by Japanese war planes which bombed and machinegunned American army and navy installations on the island of Oahu without warning; and
WHEREAS, after a fifteen minute lull, a second wave of 170 planes launched another attack at 8:40 a.m.
that lasted an hour; and
WHEREAS, more than 2,300 citizens of the United States were killed and more than 1,000 citizens of
the United States were wounded in the attack on Pearl Harbor; and
WHEREAS, nineteen ships were damaged or sunk, and 188 planes were destroyed on the ground at
nearby Wheeler Field; and
WHEREAS, the attack on Pearl Harbor marked the entry of the United States into World War II ; and
WHEREAS, the veterans of World War II and all other people of the United States commemorate
December 7th in remembrance of the attack on Pearl Harbor; and
WHEREAS, commemoration of the attack on Pearl Harbor will instill in all people of the United States a
greater understanding and appreciation of selfless sacrifice of the individuals who served in the armed
forces of the United States during World War 11.
NOW THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, that the President and the Cook County Board of
Commissioners does hereby salute the memory of the United States Servicemen who fought and died
during this sneak attack; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that Cook County facilities are urged to fly the flag of the United
States at half staff each December 7th in honor of the individuals who died as a result of their service at
Pearl Harbor.

Transmitting a Communication, dated November 15, 2000 from
JAMES L. ELDRIDGE, JR., Chief Administrative Officer, Bureau of Administration
Re:

Resolution Authorizing the Reallocation of a Portion of the 2000 Bond Volume Cap
to the Village of Wheeling, Illinois

Respectfully submitting this Resol ution for your consideration. The Village of Wheeling has requested
$900,000.00 of the 2000 Cook County Industrial Revenue Bond volume cap for the V-S Industries, Inc.
project.
The Cook County Economic Development Advisory Committee has reviewed the request and the V-S
Industries project and submits its report and recommendation of approval to cede an amount not to exceed
$450,000.00. Cook County has the recommended amount of bond cap in its unallocated year 2000 bond
cap authority. The Chief Financial Officer concurs with this recommendation.
The Village of Wheeling, intends to issue the bonds for the project on or about December 7, 2000.
Respectfu lly request approval of the Resolution to cede the bond cap to the Village of Wheeling for the
V-S Industries, Inc. project.
Ol-R-13
RESOLUTION
A Resolution Authorizing the Reallocation ofa Portion of the 2000 Volume Cap
to the Village of Wheeling, Illinois
WHEREAS, Section 146 of the Internal Revenue Code of 1986 as amended (the " Code"), grants
Illinois home rule units volume cap in the amount of $50.00 per population per year to issue private
activity bonds; and
WHEREAS, the most recent Bureau of the Census estimate of the population of the
unincorporated portion of the County of Cook, Illinois (the "County") is 129,500 giving the County a
volume cap of $6,475,000.00 for the year 2000 (the " Volume Cap" ); and
WH EREAS, the Village of Wheeling, Illinois ("Wheeling") intends to issue private act1v1ty
bonds the proceeds of which are to be used by V-S Industries, Inc. (" V-S Industries") to finance the
expansion and equipping of a manufacturing facility located in the Village of Wheeling, Illinois (the
" Wheeling Project"); and

132

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 5, 2000
WHEREAS, Wheeling has requested that the County reallocate $450,000.00 of the Volume Cap
to Wheeling to be used by Wheeling to issue private activity bonds for the financing of Wheeling Project
fo r V-S Industries because sufficient volume cap is otherwise unavailable to Wheeling; and
WHEREAS, the County has not otherwise used or reallocated more than $6,025,000.00 of its
Volume Cap prior to the date of this resolution; and
WHEREAS, pursuant to Section 6 of the Illino is Private Activity Bond Allocation Act (30 ILCS
345 I IL~ seq.) (the "Act") including, but not limited to, the written Guidelines and Procedures dated as
of January I , 2000, of the Governor' s Office of the State of Illinois issued under the Act (the "Guidelines
and Procedures"), the County may reallocate all or any portion of its Volume Cap.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOL YEO BY THE COUNTY BOARD OF THE COUNTY OF
COOK, ILLINOIS, as follows:
SECTION I : That in accordance w ith and pursuant to the power and authority granted by and
under Section 6 of Article VII of the Constitution of Illinois, Section 146 of the Code and Section 6 of the
Act, including the Guidelines and Procedures, the County, subject to Section 2 hereof, hereby reserves to
and for Wheeling and hereby irrevocably agrees to without further action by the County reallocate
$450,000.00 of the Volume Cap to Wheeling to be used to issue private activity bonds for the Wheeling
Project for V-S Industries contingent upon payment by V-S Industries to the County ofa fee of$1,000.00
on or before the date of the issuance of s uch private activity bonds.
SECTION 2: That if for any reason V-S Industries indicates by written notice to the County and
Wheeling that it does not intend to have Wheeling issue private activity bonds for the financing of
Wheeling Project, the County Board of the County (i) shall at the request and direction of V-S Industries
reallocate such unused volume cap to another municipality or state agency allowed by law for the
issuance of private acti vity bonds for the financing of Wheeling Project or (ii) may, if V-S Industries does
not request a reallocation to another municipality or state agency in its above described written notice,
reallocate such unused volume cap to another municipal ity or state agency allowed by law, in whole or in
part for any other issuance of private activity bonds or other use as permitted by law.
SECTION 3: That this Resolution sha ll constitute the agreement of the County to a different
allocation under Section 146(e )(3) of the Code and the " writing" required under Section 6 of the Act. As
required by the Act, Wheeling shall maintain in its records for the term of its bonds a record of
reallocation as described in Section I of this Resolution. Wi thin ten (I 0) calendar days of the date the
bonds are issued, Wheeling shall file or cause to be filed, in the Office of the Governor of the State of
Illinois, a confirmation of bond issuance letter relating to its bond issuance as provided in the Guidelines
and Procedures.
SECTION 4: That the County hereby covenants and warrants that it has taken no action or issued
bonds which would abrogate, dimini sh or impair its ability to fulfill the written agreement, covenants and
undertakings on its part under this Resolution.
SECTION 5: That the provisions of this Resolution are hereby declared to be separable, and if
any section, phrase or provision shall, for any reason, be declared to be invalid, such declaration shall not
affect the validity of the remainder of the sections, phrases or prov isions.
SECTION 6: That all ordinances, resolutions, orders or parts thereof in conflict with the
provisions of this Resolution are, to the extent of s uch conflict, hereby superseded.
SECTION 7: That thi s Resolution shall be effective immediately upon passage and approval, in
accordance with the law.

Transmitting a Communication, dated November 17, 2000 from
JAMES L. ELDRIDGE, JR., Chief Administrative Officer, Bureau of Administration
Re:

Bond Volume Cap Allocation for Mortgage Credit Certificates

Requesting approval of a Resolution to allocate portions of the County's 2000 Bond Volume Cap, in the
amount of $525,000.00 to the Illinois Housing Development Authority (IHDA) for the purpose of
administering a Mortgage Credit Certificate Program for suburban Cook County by December 31, 2000
in order to prevent a lapse in the bond cap authority for 2000. A lapse in bond cap authority would mean
the permanent loss of $525,000.00 to the County unless the bond cap is transferred to lHDA for the stated
purpose.
The Mortgage Credit Certificate (MCC) program allows first-time home buyers a federal income tax
credit of 25% to 50% (up to $2,000.00) of their mortgage interest a direct federal income tax credit every
year. The remaining mortgage interest may be deducted in the usual manner. A tax credit is a dollar-fordollar reduction in the tax due, not just a deduction from gross income. A MCC holder is allowed to take
tax credit each year, so long as the holder continues to live in the home for which the MCC was issued .
The MCC program eliminates the need to issue bonds and the large costs associated with such issuances.
The Department of Planning and Development coordinates and administers several housing programs.
The MCC is an opportunity to expand home ownership in coordination with the HOME Investment
Partnership Program activities, particularly to encourage new home construction in redevelopment areas.
The lllinois Housing Development Authority has administered the County's MCC program since 1994
using all of the County's allocation and addition !HOA allocations in suburban Cook at no administrative
cost to the County. The Mortgage Credit Certificate Program is available Countywide.

01-R-14
RESOLUTION
Resolution to Cede Remainder of Bond Allocation to the
Illinois Housing Development Authority for the Issuance of Mortgage Credit Certificates
WHEREAS, the County of Cook, Jllinois (the " County") is a home rule unit under Subsection (a) of
Section 6, Article Vil of the Illinois Constitution of 1970; and
WHEREAS, there exists within the County a recognized need for decent, safe, sanitary and wellconstructed housing and maintained housing which persons of low and moderate income can afford; and

134

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR DECEMBER 5, 2000
WHEREAS, the United States Government has authorized the several states and their political
subdivisions to issue qualified mortgage credit certificates (" Certificates") pursuant to Section 25 of the
Internal Revenue Code of 1986 which entitles qualifying individuals to a credit against their federal
income tax; and

WHEREAS, the Board elected to issue Certificates with County's volume cap for calendar year 2000 in
an amount not to exceed $6,432,800.00.

NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, by the President and the Board of Commissioners of the
County of Cook, Illinois ("Corporate Authorities") as follows:

Section I. Public Purpose: It is hereby found, detennined and declared that the purpose of this
Resolution is to take steps designed to reduce the cost of financing principal residences located in
the County in order to provide decent, safe and sanitary housing for qualifying persons of low and
moderate income.

Section 2. Election to Cede Remaining Allocation: The Corporate Authorities hereby cede the
remaining amount of the 2000 volume cap in the amount of $525,000.00 to the Illinois Housing
Development Authority to carry out and comply with the provisions of the Resolution concerning
Bond Volume Cap Mortgage Credit Certificates; provided that, the Illinois Housing Development
Authority shall use said Bond Volume Cap for Mortgage Credit Certificates in the County of
Cook, Illinois accordance with Section 25 ofthe Internal Revenue Code of 1986.

Section 3. Approval of Further Action: From and after the adoption of this Resolution, the
proper officials, agents and employees of the County are hereby authorized, empowered and
directed to do all such acts and things and to execute all s uch documents as may be necessary to
carry out and comply with the provi sions of this Resolution or to effectuate the purpose hereof.

Section 4. Effective Date: This Resolution shall be in full force and effect upon its passage and
approval.

Approved and adopted this 5th day of December 2000.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DA YID ORR, County Clerk

and developed that company into Metropolitan Structures, creating the largest commercial real estate firm
in the country. The firm developed many of Chicago's most recognizable buildings including One
Illinois Center, the Hyatt Regency Chicago and the Mercantile Exchange Center. Mr. Weissbourd
worked with renowned architect Ludwig Mies van der Rohe on numerous projects, and
WHEREAS, Bernard Weissbourd had a lifelong interest in urban affairs, working on issues from race
and poverty to nuclear arms. He campaigned for Harold Washington, and wrote position papers for
President Carter and presidential candidate Walter Mondale, and

Family Focus, a community-based family support program, and the Center for Transcultural Studies, and

WHEREAS, Almighty God in His infinite wisdom has called from our midst;
Gwendolyn Brooks
born into time on June 17, 191 7
passed into eternity December 3, 2000; and

as Illinois' poet laureate and the first African American woman to win the Pulitzer Prize; and
WHEREAS, Ms. Brooks grew up on Chicago's South Side and graduated from Englewood High School
and Wilson Junior College; and
WHEREAS, after graduation, her first jobs were as a maid and later as a typist; and
WHEREAS, her destiny had yet to be realized; and
WHEREAS, Ms. Brooks taught in a poetic way about the culture of the Ch icago community and in 1950
won the Pulitzer for her book length poem, Annie Allen, a ballad of African-American life in Chicago;
and
WH EREAS, Ms. Brooks was a major influence on the whole writers' movement of the '60s, '70s and
' 80s; and
WHEREAS, Ms. Brooks created and funded a Poet Laureate Award that recognized talented student
poets from elementary and high schools throughout Illinois; and
WH EREAS, the Pulitzer Prize winner authored 22 books and her most recent work, In Birmingham, will
be published early next year; and
WHEREAS, the message Ms. Brooks tried to deliver was to look at oneself, into one's soul to discover
who you really are, and to always stand up to evil and injustice everywhere it exists; and
WHEREAS, Ms. Brooks had a strong literary voice and was called a "giant in American Literature". She
will be dearly missed for the light and beauty of her poems, the hunger for justice that infused her life's
work and for her quest to offer the gift of poetry.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners does hereby
express its deep sorrow at the death of Gwendolyn Brooks and offers its heartfelt sympathy to her family
in their hour of sorrow and joins them in honoring her memory; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be tendered to the family of
Gwendolyn Brooks as a memorial of her good works and spread upon the official proceed ings of this
Honorable Body.
Approved and adopted this 5th day of December 2000.

Ol-R-27
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE CARL R. HANSEN, COUNTY COMMISSIONER
ELECTION SYSTEM
WHEREAS, the recent general election on November 7th disclosed some problems with the recording of
votes, and
WHEREAS, s uch problems may have affected both the number of votes on candidates and referenda as
well as retention votes for the judiciary, and
WHEREAS, at least some of such problems may be lessened by use of electronic rejection of
questionable ballots, and
WHEREAS, s uch electronic rejection of questionable ballots is already provided for in the program of
Cook County voting equipment, and
WHEREAS, Cook County cannot use such program without the approval of the Illinois General
Assembly, and
WHEREAS, design, structure and other aspects of the voting process require rev iew, now therefore
BE IT RESOLVED, that the General Assembly be urged to allow use of programs and equipment already
purchased for the citizens of Cook County, and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that all aspects of accurately recording votes cast, to include the
formation and the stability of the punch card ballot, be reviewed by the Cook County Clerk and reported
to the Cook County Board of Commissioners as soon as possible.
Approved and adopted this 5th day of December.
JOHN H. STROGER JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DA YID ORR, County Clerk

PUBLIC TESTIMONY
Pursuant to Rule 4-30, John Klaczak, Fire Chief of the Village of Thornton and President of Midwest
Bio-Reclamation, Inc. (MBR), addressed the President and Members of the Cook County Board of
Commissioners. Mr. Klaczak expressed concern regarding the transportation of deceased bodies to the
county morgue.

ADJOURNMENT
Commissioner Butler, seconded by Comm issioner Daley, moved that the meeting do now adjourn to meet
again at the same time and same place on Tuesday, December 19, 2000, in accordance with County Board
Resolution 00-R-9.
The motion prevailed and the meeting stood adjourned.
